The Definition of Contradictory and its Refinement
Author lists contradictory pairs and defines contradictory as removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any categorical proposition by negating the entire proposition and recognize the technical refinement regarding 'removal'.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a proposition is its negation—but does 'negation' mean removal or opposite?

In this passage, the author gives a straightforward rule: the contradictory of any proposition is its 'removal' (negation). However, the commentator Sharif points out that technically, affirmation is not the removal of negation but its contradictory. This lesson unpacks the general definition and the logical nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's general rule
The author says: 'نقيض كلّ شيء رفعه' (the contradictory of everything is its removal). Understand that 'removal' here means negation of the whole proposition.
2
Apply the rule to a categorical proposition
Take the example: 'كل إنسان حيوان بالضرورة' (Every human is an animal necessarily). Its contradictory is 'ليس كذلك' (it is not so), i.e., the whole proposition is negated.
3
Examine Sharif's refinement
The commentator objects: technically, negation is the removal of affirmation, but affirmation is not the removal of negation; rather, it is the contradictory. So the rule holds only if 'removal' is taken broadly to mean 'opposite'.
4
Understand the broad interpretation
Recognise that the author's statement is true if 'رفع' is interpreted as what is equivalent to the contradictory (i.e., the opposite truth-value). This resolves the technical issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: فنقيض الضرورية المطلقة الممكنة العامة، لأن سلب الضرورة مع الضرورة مما يتناقضان جزماً.
ونقيض الدائمة المطلقة المطلقة العامّة، لأنّ السلب في كل الأوقات ينافيه الإيجاب في البعض وبالعكس، ونقيض المشروطة العامة الحينية الممكنة، أعني التي حكم فيها برفع الضرورة بحسب الوصف عن الجانب المخالف، كقولنا: كل من به ذات الجنب يمكن أن يسعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوباً». ونقيض العرفية العامة الحينية المطلقة، أعني التي حكم فيها بثبوت المحمول للموضوع أو سلبه عنه في بعض أحيان وصف الموضوع، ومثالها مامر.
أقول : أعلم أولا أن نقيض كلّ شيء رفعه، وهذا القدر كاف في أخذ النقيض لقضية قضيّة حتى أن كل قضية يكون نقيضها رفع تلك القضية.
فإذا قلنا : كلّ إنسان حيوان بالضرورة» فنقيضها أنه ليس كذلك، وكذلك في سائر القضايا، لكن إذا رفع القضيّة فربما يكون نفس رفعها
(۱) فيه مناقشة، لأن السلب شيء ونقيضه الإيجاب، وليس الإيجاب رفع السلب وإن كان مستلزماً له، بل السلب رفع الإيجاب، فالأولى أن يقال : رفع كلّ شيء نقيضه؛ إلا أن يريد بالرفع ما هو أعم من الرفع حقيقة وما هو مساو له، وبالنقيض ما هو أعم من النقيض حقيقة وما يساويه، فيظهر حينئذ صدق قوله : «نقيض كل شيء رفعه» (شريف).
He said: The contradictory of the absolute necessary is the general possible, because the negation of necessity with necessity are contradictory per se. The contradictory of the absolute perpetual is the absolute general, because the negation in all times contradicts affirmation in some and vice versa. The contradictory of the general conditional is the temporal possible, i.e. the one in which judgment is made of the removal of necessity according to the description from the opposite side, like our saying: 'Everyone who has pleurisy can cough in some times of his being pleuritic.' The contradictory of the general customary is the absolute temporal, i.e. the one in which judgment is made of the affirmation of the predicate for the subject or its negation in some times of the subject's description, and its example has passed. I say: Know first that the contradictory of everything is its removal, and this much is sufficient for taking the contradictory of a proposition by proposition, so that the contradictory of every proposition is the removal of that proposition. So if we say: 'Every human is an animal necessarily,' its contradictory is that it is not so, and likewise in all propositions. But when the proposition is removed, sometimes its removal itself [needs qualification] (1) There is a discussion about it, because negation is something and its contradictory is affirmation, and affirmation is not the removal of negation, although it implies it; rather negation is the removal of affirmation. So it is better to say: The removal of everything is its contradictory; unless by 'removal' he means what is more general than actual removal and what is equivalent to it, and by 'contradictory' what is more general than actual contradictory and what is equivalent to it; then his statement 'the contradictory of everything is its removal' would be true. (Sharif)
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage first lists the specific contradictories of several types of modal propositions: (1) The contradictory of a necessary proposition (e.g., 'Every human is a writer necessarily') is a possible proposition with a negative quantifier (e.g., 'Not every human is a writer possibly'). (2) The contradictory of a perpetual proposition (holding at all times) is a general absolute proposition that negates in all times, because affirming in some times contradicts. (3) The contradictory of a general conditional (e.g., 'Every pleuritic person breathes painfully while he has pleurisy') is a temporal possible proposition that allows the opposite at some times. (4) The contradictory of a general customary (e.g., 'Every human moves when he grows') is an absolute temporal proposition that holds only at some times. The author then gives a general definition: 'The contradictory of every proposition is its removal' (i.e., its negation). He illustrates with an example. The marginal note from Sharif refines this: technically, the contradictory of a negation is an affirmation, not the 'removal' of the negation; but if 'removal' is taken broadly to mean 'opposite', the statement holds.

Key Terms
النقيض
الرفع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'كل إنسان ليس حيوانا بالضرورة'
C) 'بعض إنسان ليس حيوانا بالضرورة'
D) 'لا إنسان حيوان بالضرورة'

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a proposition is its negation (removal), but technically, 'removal' must be understood broadly as 'opposite truth-value' to avoid a subtle logical error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Take the proposition 'Every intoxicant is forbidden necessarily.' Write its contradictory using the general rule.

Contradictories of Modal Propositions: Application to Four Types
Author lists contradictory pairs for four modal propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the correct contradictory of a given modal proposition (necessary, perpetual, conditional, customary).

Core Idea
Each modal type has a specific contradictory that negates both the modality and the temporal scope.

The author provides a list of contradictory pairs for four types of modal propositions: absolute necessary, absolute perpetual, general conditional, and general customary. By examining these examples, we learn that the contradictory must be of a different modality and often with a different quantifier or temporal condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modal types listed
The passage mentions: الضرورية المطلقة (absolute necessary), الدائمة المطلقة (absolute perpetual), المشروطة العامة (general conditional), العرفية العامة (general customary).
2
Extract the contradictory for each type
For necessary, it's الممكنة العامة (general possible); for perpetual, it's المطلقة العامة (absolute general); for conditional, it's الحينية الممكنة (temporal possible); for customary, it's الحينية المطلقة (absolute temporal).
3
Understand the rationale
The author explains why: e.g., negation of necessity with necessity are contradictory; negation in all times contradicts affirmation in some.
4
Apply to an example
Take a necessary proposition: 'كل إنسان حيوان بالضرورة' – its contradictory is 'ليس كل إنسان حيوان بالضرورة' which is a general possible (i.e., it is possibly not the case). Similarly, for a perpetual proposition like 'النار حارة في كل الأوقات' (Fire is hot at all times), its contradictory is 'ليس النار حارة في كل الأوقات' (Fire is not hot at all times), which is an absolute general.
The examples are from the passage's logic; for Islamic topics, use 'كل فريضة واجبة بالضرورة' (Every obligation is necessary) etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The contradictory of the absolute perpetual is the absolute general, because the negation in all times contradicts affirmation in some and vice versa. The contradictory of the general conditional is the temporal possible, i.e. the one in which judgment is made of the removal of necessity according to the description from the opposite side, like our saying: 'Everyone who has pleurisy can cough in some times of his being pleuritic.' (Sharif)

Identifying Contradictories of Modal Propositions
Author lists the contradictories for absolute necessary, perpetual, conditional, and common custom modal propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory for each of the four modal propositions: absolute necessary, absolute perpetual, general conditional, and general common custom.

Core Idea
Every modal proposition has a specific contradictory that flips both quantity and modality.

In this passage, the author provides the contradictory for each of the four main modal proposition types. Knowing these pairings is essential for performing valid immediate inferences in Islamic logic. We will work through each rule step by step, starting with the absolute necessary and ending with the general common custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four modal types
List the four modal propositions discussed: absolute necessary (ضرورية مطلقة), absolute perpetual (دائمة مطلقة), general conditional (مشروطة عامة حينية), and general common custom (عرفية عامة حينية). Note that each has a universal affirmative form with a specific temporal modality.
The passage gives the Arabic names; match them with the examples provided.
2
For each type, locate its contradictory
The author explicitly names the contradictory for each. For absolute necessary it is absolute possible (ممكنة عامة). For absolute perpetual it is absolute general (مطلقة عامة). For general conditional it is possible (ممكنة). For general common custom it is absolute (مطلقة). Write down each contradictory term.
Pay attention to the modality and quantity shift: universal to particular, and necessity to possibility or permanence to non-permanence.
3
Verify the contradictory relationship
Check that the contradictory satisfies the logical condition: both cannot be true and both cannot be false. For example, the negation of necessity is possibility, and universal affirmative contradicts particular negative. The passage gives the reason: 'negation of necessity together with necessity are inherently contradictory.'
This verification is a mental check; the author assumes the reader knows the definition of contradictory.
4
Apply the rule to an example
Take the example of absolute necessary: 'كل إنسان حيوان بالضرورة' (Every human is necessarily an animal). Its contradictory is 'بعض الإنسان ليس بحيوان بالإمكان العام' (Some human is possibly not an animal). Confirm that the modality changed from necessary to possible and the quantifier from universal to particular negative.
Use the example from the passage for the conditional: 'كل من به ذات الجنب يمكن أن يسعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوبًا' as the contradictory of the conditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۱ - نقيض الموجهات الضرورية والدائمة المطلقتين والعرفية والمشروطة العامتين]
قال: فنقيض الضرورية المطلقة الممكنة العامة، لأن سلب الضرورة مع الضرورة مما يتناقضان جزماً.
ونقيض الدائمة المطلقة المطلقة العامّة، لأنّ السلب في كل الأوقات ينافيه الإيجاب في البعض وبالعكس، ونقيض المشروطة العامة الحينية الممكنة، أعني التي حكم فيها برفع الضرورة بحسب الوصف عن الجانب المخالف، كقولنا: كل من به ذات الجنب يمكن أن يسعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوباً». ونقيض العرفية العامة الحينية المطلقة، أعني التي حكم فيها بثبوت المحمول للموضوع أو سلبه عنه في بعض أحيان وصف الموضوع، ومثالها مامر.
[71 - The contradictory of the necessary, perpetual absolute, common custom, and conditional general propositions] He said: So the contradictory of the absolute necessary is the absolute possible, because the negation of necessity together with necessity are inherently contradictory. And the contradictory of the absolute perpetual is the absolute general, because negation in all times contradicts affirmation in some times and vice versa. And the contradictory of the general conditional (temporal) is the possible, meaning that in which the removal of necessity according to the description from the opposite side is judged, like our statement: 'Everyone who has pleurisy can cough in some time of his being pleuritic.' And the contradictory of the general common custom (temporal) is the absolute, meaning that in which the affirmation of the predicate for the subject or its negation in some times of the subject's description is judged, and its example is what has passed.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictories for four main types of modal propositions. It begins with the absolute necessary (الضرورية المطلقة), which is a universal affirmative with necessity, e.g., 'Every human is necessarily an animal.' Its contradictory is the absolute possible (الممكنة العامة), which is a particular negative with possibility: 'Some human is possibly not an animal.' The reason given is that the negation of necessity is inherently contradictory to necessity. Next, the absolute perpetual (الدائمة المطلقة) is a proposition that holds at all times, e.g., 'Every raven is black at all times.' Its contradictory is the absolute general (المطلقة العامة), which is a particular negative with absolute (non-modal) form, because perpetuity in all times contradicts the affirmation in some times. Then the general conditional temporal (المشروطة العامة الحينية) is a proposition that holds only as long as the subject has a certain description, e.g., 'Everyone with pleurisy coughs' while having pleurisy. Its contradictory is the possible (الممكنة) which removes necessity regarding that description, as in 'Everyone with pleurisy can cough sometimes while having pleurisy.' Finally, the general common custom (العرفية العامة الحينية) is a proposition that holds in some times of the subject's description, e.g., 'Some writer writes at some time of his being a writer.' Its contradictory is the absolute (المطلقة), which is a universal negative with absolute form. The passage provides the rules without deriving them from first principles.

Key Terms
نقيض
ضرورية مطلقة
ممكنة عامة
دائمة مطلقة
مطلقة عامة
مشروطة عامة حينية
عرفية عامة حينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) لا إنسان حيوان بالضرورة
B) بعض الإنسان ليس بحيوان بالإمكان العام
C) بعض الإنسان حيوان بالإمكان العام
D) كل إنسان حيوان بالإمكان العام

Key Takeaway
Each modal proposition has a unique contradictory that negates both the modality and the quantifier, ensuring immediate inference validity.

Determining the Contradictory of Modal Propositions
Author defines the concept of contradictory in modal propositions and specifies the contradictory pairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any modal proposition (necessary, perpetual, general possible) by applying the rules of necessary equivalents.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a modal proposition is its necessary equivalent, not always its direct negation.

In Islamic logic, modal propositions are statements qualified by necessity, possibility, or perpetuity. Determining their contradictories is essential for constructing valid arguments and refutations. However, as Qutbi explains in this passage, the contradictory of a modal proposition is not always its straightforward negation; sometimes we need to use a necessary equivalent to have a determinate concept. This lesson will guide you through identifying the contradictory of necessary and perpetual propositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modal type
Determine if the proposition is necessary (daruriyya), perpetual (da'ima), or absolute. Also note its quantity (universal or particular).
Necessary propositions assert that the predicate holds necessarily at all times; perpetual asserts it holds at all times without necessity.
2
Find the direct contradictory or its equivalent
For necessary propositions, the contradictory is the general possible (mumkina 'amma) of opposite quality and quantity. For perpetual, it is the absolute general (mutlaqa 'amma) of opposite quality and quantity.
The author emphasizes that the general possible is a necessary equivalent of the direct contradictory when the direct negation lacks a determinate concept.
3
Apply the rule to the four quantified forms
Using the table given: universal affirmative necessary contradicts particular negative general possible; universal negative necessary contradicts particular affirmative general possible; etc. Memorize these pairs.
The same pattern applies for perpetual with absolute general.
4
Practice with examples to internalize
Take a necessary proposition like 'Every A is necessarily B' and form its contradictory: 'Some A is possibly not B' (general possible particular negative).
Also practice with perpetual: 'Every A is perpetually B' contradicts 'Some A is not B at some time' (absolute particular negative).

فالمراد بالنقيض في هذا الفصل أحد الأمرين : إما نفس النقيض أو لازمه المساوي.
و إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : نقيض الضرورية المطلقة الممكنة العامة :
(1) الإمكان العام وإن كان نقيضاً حقيقياً للضرورية الذاتية - بناء على ما مر من أن الإمكان العام سلب الضرورة الذاتية من الجانب المخالف للحكم - لكن من حيث اعتبار الكمية تكون الممكنة العامة مساوية لنقيض الضرورية، فإن نقيض الموجبة الكلية هو رفعها على ماذكر ، وليس رفعها عين مفهوم السالبة الجزئية، بل هو لازم مساو لمفهوم السالبة الجزئية، وعليـه فقـس سـائر المحصورات، فالمعتبر من النقيض في هذا الفصل ليس إلا ما يكون لازماً مساوياً لما هو النقيض الحقيقي لا ما يكون أحد هذين الأمرين كمازعم، وإن أردت التفصيل في تعيين نقائض القضايا فضع المحصورات الأربع للضرورية و ضع المحصورات الأربع للممكنة العامة، ثم اعتبر التناقض فتجد نقيض الموجبة الكلية الضرورية : السالبة الجزئية الممكنة العامة، وبالعكس؛ ونقيض السالبة الكلية الضرورية : الموجبة الجزئية الممكنة العامة، وبالعكس؛ ونقيض الموجبة الجزئية الضرورية : السالبة الكلّيّة الممكنة العامة، وبالعكس؛ ونقيض السالبة الجزئية الضرورية : الموجبة الكلية الممكنة العامة، وبالعكس،
لأن الإمكان العام هو سلب الضرورة عن الجانب المخالف للحكم، ولاخفاء في أن إثبات الضرورة في الجانب المخالف وسلبها في ذلك الجانب مما يتناقضان.
فضرورة الإيجاب نقيضها سلب ضرورة الإيجاب، وسلب ضرورة الإيجاب هو بعينه إمكان عام سالب.
وضرورة السلب نقيضها سلب ضرورة السلب، و هو بعينه إمكان عام موجب.
وكذلك إمكان الإيجاب نقيضه سلب إمكان الإيجاب : أي سلب سلب ضرورة السلب الذي هو بعينه ضرورة السلب. وإمكان السلب نقيضه سلب إمكان السلب - أي سلب سلب ضرورة الإيجاب الذي هو بعينه ضرورة الإيجاب.
ونقيض الدائمة المطلقة المطلقة العامة، لأن السلب في كل الأوقات ينافيه الإيجاب في البعض، وبالعكس - أي الإيجاب في كل الأوقات ينافيه السلب في البعض.
وإنما قال: "ينافيه" - بخلاف ماقال في الضرورية - لأن إطلاق الإيجاب لا يناقض دوام السلب بل يلازم نقيضه، فإن دوام السلب نقيضه رفع دوام السلب، ويلزمه إطلاق الإيجاب، لأنه إذا لم يكن المحمول دائم

Contradiction: A proposition that has a determinate conceptual content for the mind, from among the considered propositions. And sometimes its negation is not a proposition that has a determinate conceptual content for the mind from among the propositions, but rather its negation has a necessary equivalent that has a determinate conceptual content for the mind from among the propositions. So that necessary equivalent is taken and the name 'contradictory' is applied to it metaphorically, so that for the contradictories of propositions, determinate conceptual contents for the mind are obtained. And these concepts were obtained, and they were not satisfied with the summary capacity in taking the contradictory, in order to facilitate their use in judgments. So what is meant by 'contradictory' in this chapter is one of two things: either the actual contradictory itself or its necessary equivalent. And if you know this, we say: The contradictory of the absolute necessary [proposition] is the general possible [proposition]. (1) General possibility, even though it is a true contradictory of the essential necessary - based on what has passed that general possibility is the negation of essential necessity from the side opposite to the judgment - nevertheless, from the perspective of considering quantity, the general possible is equivalent to the contradictory of the necessary. For the contradictory of the universal affirmative is its negation as mentioned, and its negation is not identical to the concept of the particular negative; rather it is a necessary equivalent to the concept of the particular negative. And upon this, measure the rest of the quantified [propositions]. So what is considered from the contradictory in this chapter is only what is a necessary equivalent to what is the true contradictory, not that it is one of these two things as was claimed. And if you desire detail in specifying the contradictories of propositions, then place the four quantified [propositions] for the necessary and place the four quantified [propositions] for the general possible, then consider the contradiction, and you will find: the contradictory of the necessary universal affirmative is the general possible particular negative, and vice versa; and the contradictory of the necessary universal negative is the general possible particular affirmative, and vice versa; and the contradictory of the necessary particular affirmative is the general possible universal negative, and vice versa; and the contradictory of the necessary particular negative is the general possible universal affirmative, and vice versa. Because general possibility is the negation of necessity from the side opposite to the judgment, and it is not hidden that affirming necessity in the opposite side and negating it in that side are contradictory to each other. So necessity of affirmation: its contradictory is the negation of necessity of affirmation, and the negation of necessity of affirmation is exactly a negative general possibility. And necessity of negation: its contradictory is the negation of necessity of negation, and it is exactly an affirmative general possibility. Likewise, possibility of affirmation: its contradictory is the negation of possibility of affirmation, i.e., the negation of the negation of necessity of negation, which is exactly necessity of negation. And possibility of negation: its contradictory is the negation of possibility of negation, i.e., the negation of the negation of necessity of affirmation, which is exactly necessity of affirmation. And the contradictory of the perpetual [proposition] is the absolute absolute [proposition]? Actually, the text says 'the contradictory of the perpetual is the absolute absolute'? It says: 'the contradictory of the perpetual (al-da'ima) is the absolute absolute (al-mutlaqa al-'amma?)' It says: 'And the contradictory of the perpetual (da'ima) is the absolute general (mutlaqa 'amma)'? The Arabic says: 'ونقيض الدائمة المطلقة المطلقة العامة' which might be 'wa-naqid al-da'ima al-mutlaqa al-'amma' but it's ambiguous. The translation continues: because negation in all times contradicts affirmation in some parts, and vice versa - i.e., affirmation in all times contradicts negation in some parts. And he only said 'contradicts' - unlike what he said in the necessary - because absolute affirmation does not contradict perpetual negation but rather entails its contradictory. For perpetual negation, its contradictory is the negation of perpetual negation, and absolute affirmation entails it, because if the predicate is not perpetual... And thus is the case between the perpetual and the absolute general, and between every proposition and what is made its contradictory - so reflect on it (Sharif).
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage from Qutbi's commentary on al-Shamsiyya clarifies the concept of the contradictory (naqid) in modal propositions. The author first notes that sometimes the direct negation of a proposition lacks a determinate concept, so its necessary equivalent (lazim musawi) is used metaphorically as the contradictory. Thus, in this chapter, 'contradictory' refers either to the actual contradictory or its equivalent. The main discussion concerns the contradictory of necessary (daruriyya) propositions. It is stated that the general possible (mumkina 'amma) is the true contradictory of the essential necessary, but considering quantity, the general possible is equivalent to the contradictory of the necessary. For example, the contradictory of a universal affirmative necessary proposition is not the particular negative per se, but its necessary equivalent, which is the general possible particular negative. The author then provides the full set of four contradictory pairs: the necessary universal affirmative contradicts the general possible particular negative, the necessary universal negative contradicts the general possible particular affirmative, the necessary particular affirmative contradicts the general possible universal negative, and the necessary particular negative contradicts the general possible universal affirmative. The reason is that general possibility is defined as the negation of necessity from the opposite side of the judgment, and affirming necessity contradicts negating it in the same side. Then, the author analyzes the internal relations: necessity of affirmation (i.e., a necessary affirmative) has as its contradictory the negation of necessity of affirmation, which is exactly a negative general possible; similarly, necessity of negation has as its contradictory a positive general possible. For possibility of affirmation, its contradictory is the negation of possibility of affirmation, which reduces to necessity of negation; and possibility of negation reduces to necessity of affirmation. Finally, the contradictory of the perpetual (da'ima) proposition is the absolute general (mutlaqa 'amma). Perpetual negation (i.e., never being the case) contradicts affirmative in some part, and vice versa. The author notes that here he uses 'contradicts' (yunafihi) rather than 'is the contradictory' because absolute affirmation does not directly contradict perpetual negation but entails its contradictory. The passage ends with an exhortation to reflect, likely from the commentator Sharif (al-Jurjani).

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a modal proposition is not always its direct negation; when the direct negation lacks a determinate concept, its necessary equivalent is used as the contradictory.

The Contradictories of Modal Propositions
Defines contradictions of modal propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory (nāqid) of any necessary or possible categorical proposition.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a necessary proposition is always a possible negative, not a necessary opposite.

In Islamic logic, modal propositions (al-ḍarūrati wa al-imkāni) have precise contradictories. This passage from al-Qutb al-Taḥtānī explains how necessity and possibility relate through negation. Understanding these contradictions is essential for constructing valid arguments in kalām and uṣūl al-fiqh, where modal distinctions like 'necessarily' and 'possibly' determine the strength of claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modal operator and quality
Look for whether the proposition uses 'necessarily' (ḍarūra) or 'possibly' (imkān), and whether it is affirmative (ījāb) or negative (salb). For example, 'Necessarily, every A is B' is a necessary affirmative.
2
Apply the rule for necessity
The contradictory of a necessary affirmative is a possible negative. That is, negating the necessity and flipping the quality. For 'Necessarily, every A is B', the contradictory is 'Possibly, some A is not B'.
3
Apply the rule for possibility
The contradictory of a possible affirmative is a necessary negative. This follows from double negation: negating possibility (which itself is a negation of necessity) yields necessity of the opposite. For 'Possibly, some A is B', the contradictory is 'Necessarily, no A is B'.
4
Verify using the modal square of opposition
Check that the original and its contradictory satisfy the two conditions: they cannot both be true and they cannot both be false. This confirms the relationship is genuine contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن الإمكان العام هو سلب الضرورة عن الجانب المخالف للحكم، ولاخفاء في أن إثبات الضرورة في الجانب المخالف وسلبها في ذلك الجانب مما يتناقضان. فضرورة الإيجاب نقيضها سلب ضرورة الإيجاب، وسلب ضرورة الإيجاب هو بعينه إمكان عام سالب. وضرورة السلب نقيضها سلب ضرورة السلب، وهو بعينه إمكان عام موجب. وكذلك إمكان الإيجاب نقيضه سلب إمكان الإيجاب: أي سلب سلب ضرورة السلب الذي هو بعينه ضرورة السلب. وإمكان السلب نقيضه سلب إمكان السلب - أي سلب سلب ضرورة الإيجاب الذي هو بعينه ضرورة الإيجاب.
Because absolute possibility is the negation of necessity from the side opposite to the judgment, and it is no secret that affirming necessity in the opposite side and negating it in that side are contradictory. So the necessity of affirmation, its contradictory is the negation of necessity of affirmation, and the negation of necessity of affirmation is precisely absolute possible negative. And the necessity of negation, its contradictory is the negation of necessity of negation, and it is precisely absolute possible affirmative. Similarly, the possibility of affirmation, its contradictory is the negation of possibility of affirmation, i.e., the negation of the negation of necessity of negation, which is precisely the necessity of negation. And the possibility of negation, its contradictory is the negation of possibility of negation, i.e., the negation of the negation of necessity of affirmation, which is precisely the necessity of affirmation.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory pairs (nāqid) of modal propositions. The author begins by stating that absolute possibility (imkān ʿāmm) is the negation of necessity from the side opposite the judgment. He then explains that the contradictory of a necessary affirmative (ḍarūrat al-ījāb) is the negation of that necessity, which is exactly an absolute possible negative (imkān ʿāmm sālib). Similarly, the contradictory of a necessary negative is an absolute possible affirmative. Next, he treats the possibility propositions: the contradictory of a possible affirmative (imkān al-ījāb) is the negation of that possibility, which after double negation yields the necessity of negation (ḍarūrat as-salbi). Likewise, the contradictory of a possible negative yields the necessity of affirmation. The point is to show how modal propositions form a square of opposition with clear contradictions.

Key Terms
ضرورة (ḍarūra): Necessity of a judgment; a modal operator indicating that the predicate holds necessarily for the subject.
إمكان (imkān): Possibility; the modal operator indicating that the predicate may or may not hold for the subject.
نقيض (nāqid): Contradictory; a proposition that is opposite in truth value in all cases.
سلب (salb): Negation; the act of denying the predicate of the subject.
إيجاب (ījāb): Affirmation; the act of asserting the predicate of the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Necessarily, no A is B
B) Possibly, some A is not B
C) Necessarily, some A is not B
D) Possibly, every A is B

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a necessary proposition is always a possible proposition with the opposite quality (affirmative/negative), and vice versa.

Negation of Perpetual and Absolute General Propositions
Explains negation relationship between perpetual and absolute general propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory and repulsive relationships between perpetual and absolute general temporal propositions in immediate inference.

Core Idea
Perpetual and absolute general propositions relate by repulsion, not direct contradiction.

In this passage, the author delves into the subtle opposition between perpetual (dāʾima) and absolute general (muṭlaqa ʿāmma) propositions. While we often think of contradictories as direct negations, here the relationship is mediated by entailment. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly evaluating temporal modal claims in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Define the two temporal modalities
A perpetual proposition (دائمة) asserts that the predicate holds for the subject at all times (e.g., 'A is B always'). An absolute general proposition (مطلقة عامة) asserts that the predicate holds at least once (e.g., 'A is B at some time'). Recognize that 'absolute general' can be affirmative or negative.
These are not the same as universal and particular in subject-quantifier logic; they are temporal modalities.
2
Identify the contradictory claim
The author states: the contradictory of the perpetual is the absolute general. More precisely, the contradictory of a perpetual affirmative (e.g., 'A is B always') is an absolute negative ('A is not B at some time'); the contradictory of a perpetual negative ('A is never B') is an absolute affirmative ('A is B at some time'). Conversely, the contradictory of an absolute affirmative is a perpetual negative, and of an absolute negative is a perpetual affirmative.
Note the symmetry: the contradictory flips both quality and temporal scope.
3
Understand the repulsion (munāfāt) nuance
The author uses 'repels' (yunāfī) instead of 'contradicts' (yanāquḍ) because absolute affirmation does not directly contradict perpetual negation; rather, it entails the contradictory of perpetual negation. For instance, 'A is B at some time' does not directly oppose 'A is never B' but entails 'It is not the case that A is never B'.
This subtlety avoids confusion when mapping logical relationships between temporal propositions.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Consider the perpetual proposition 'Every obligation is permanent.' Its contradictory is 'Some obligation is not permanent at some time' (absolute negative). Verify that the negation of the perpetual leads to the absolute, and that the absolute does not directly contradict the perpetual but rather repels it.
Use examples from Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh) to solidify understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التناقض ونقيض الدائمة المطلقة المطلقة العامة، لأن السلب في كل الأوقات ينافيه الإيجاب في البعض، وبالعكس - أي الإيجاب في كل الأوقات ينافيه السلب في البعض. وإنما قال: «ينافيه» - بخلاف ماقال في الضرورية - لأن إطلاق الإيجاب لا يناقض دوام السلب بل يلازم نقيضه، فإن دوام السلب نقيضه رفع دوام السلب، ويلزمه إطلاق الإيجاب، لأنه إذا لم يكن المحمول دائم السلب لكان إما دائم الإيجاب أو ثابتاً في بعض الأوقات دون بعض، وأيا ما كان يتحقق إطلاق الإيجاب. وكذلك دوام الإيجاب يناقضه رفع دوام الإيجاب، وإذا ارتفع دوام الإيجاب، فإما أن يدوم السلب أو يتحقق السلب في بعض الأوقات دون بعض، وعلى كلا التقديرين فإطلاق السلب لازم جزماً. و هكذا البيان في أن نقيض المطلقة العامة الدائمة المطلقة، فإنه إذا لم يكن الإيجاب في الجملة يلزم السلب دائماً، وإذا لم يكن السلب في الجملة يلزم الإيجاب دائماً. فتأمل فيها (شريف).
Contradiction. And the contradictory of the perpetual is the absolute general, because negation in all times is repelled by affirmation in some, and vice versa – i.e., affirmation in all times is repelled by negation in some. And he only said 'repels' – unlike what he said in the necessary – because absolute affirmation does not contradict perpetual negation but entails its contradictory. For perpetual negation, its contradictory is the removal of perpetual negation, and it entails absolute affirmation, because if the predicate is not perpetually negated, then it is either perpetually affirmed or established in some times and not others; in either case absolute affirmation is realized. Similarly, perpetual affirmation is contradicted by the removal of perpetual affirmation; and if perpetual affirmation is removed, then either negation is perpetual or negation occurs in some times and not others; on both suppositions absolute negation necessarily follows. And similarly, the explanation that the contradictory of the absolute general is the perpetual absolute: if there is no affirmation at all, perpetual negation follows; and if there is no negation at all, perpetual affirmation follows. So reflect on this (Sharif).
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage clarifies the contradiction (tanāquḍ) relation between the perpetual (dāʾima) and the absolute general (muṭlaqa ʿāmma). The author first states that the contradictory of a perpetual proposition is an absolute general proposition. He then explains the subtlety: perpetual negation (negation in all times) is repelled (yunāfīhi) by affirmation in some times, not strictly contradicted. The reason is that absolute affirmation (i.e., affirmation in at least one time) is not the direct contradictory of perpetual negation but rather entails its contradictory. For example, the contradictory of 'never A is B' is not 'sometimes A is B' but rather 'at least once A is B' (absolute affirmation). However, absolute affirmation is logically equivalent to the contradictory of perpetual negation. The same logic applies to perpetual affirmation and absolute negation. The passage emphasizes that the relationship is one of repulsion (munāfāt) rather than strict contradiction (munāqaḍa) because the opposition is not direct but mediated by entailment. The author invites the reader to reflect carefully.

Key Terms
دائمة
مطلقة عامة
ينافيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because perpetual negation and absolute affirmation are not mutually exclusive
B) Because absolute affirmation entails the contradictory of perpetual negation, not directly contradicts it
C) Because the author made a mistake
D) Because perpetual and absolute general are identical

Key Takeaway
Perpetual and absolute general propositions are repulsive opposites, not direct contradictories; the correct contradictory of a perpetual affirmative is an absolute negative, and vice versa.

Finding the Correct Contradictory for Non-Standard Modal Propositions
Author defines and compares the negations of conditional and conventional general propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory (nāqiḍ) for conditional general and conventional general propositions and distinguish them from standard contradictions.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conditional general is a temporal possible, not a standard simple proposition.

In this passage, the author extends the theory of contradictories to two specific types of modal propositions: the conditional general (mashrūṭa ʿāmma) and the conventional general (ʿurfiyya ʿāmma). Unlike the familiar simple propositions (e.g., essential necessary, perpetual), these do not have well-known contradictory forms. The author explains that their contradictories are special temporal propositions that must be carefully constructed to respect both modality and quantity. Understanding these subtleties is essential for rigorous argumentation in the Islamic sciences, where modal distinctions often carry theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two target propositions
Locate in the Arabic the terms 'mashrūṭa ʿāmma' (conditional general) and 'ʿurfiyya ʿāmma' (conventional general). For each, note that they involve a condition or custom, not absolute necessity or perpetuity.
2
Examine the example of a conditional general contradiction
The author gives: 'Every person with pleurisy possibly coughs at some times while afflicted.' This is a temporal possible (ḥīniyya mumkina). Understand that it negates necessity under the description (not at all times, but only when the condition holds).
3
Compare with standard contradiction patterns
The author compares: temporal possible : conditional general :: absolute possible : necessary. The temporal possible is a true modal contradictory for the conditional general, just as the absolute possible is for the necessary.
4
Analyze the conventional general contradiction
The author states that the temporal absolute (ḥīniyya muṭlaqa) is not a true contradictory of the conventional general, but a necessary equivalent. This means it does not negate the original in modality perfectly, but is always equivalent to its negation.
5
Note the quantity caveat
The author concludes that none of these are true contradictions regarding quantity (i.e., the universal-particular relation does not hold). This is because these propositions involve additional temporal or conditional qualifiers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقيض المشروطة العامة الحينية الممكنة، وهي التي يحكم فيها بسلب الضرورة بحسب الوصف عن الجانب المخالف، كقولنا: «كل من به ذات الجنب يمكن أن يسعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوباً» وذلك لأن هذه قضية بسيطة لم تعتبر في القضايا البسيطة المشهورة واحتيج إليها في نقيض بعض البسائط المشهورة، فالقضية الضرورية الذاتية ونقيضها - أعني الممكنة العامة - كلتاهما من البسائط المشهورة وكذا الدائمة والمطلقة العامة؛ وأما المشروطة العامة فليس نقيضها من القضايا المشهورة، وكذا نقيض العرفية العامة. ونسبة الحينية الممكنة إلى المشروطة العامة كنسبة الممكنة العامة إلى الضرورية في أنها نقيض المشروطة حقيقة بحسب الجهة، ونسبة الحينية المطلقة إلى العرفية العامة كنسبة المطلقة العامة إلى الدائمة في أنها ليست نقيض العرفية حقيقة بحسب الجهة، بل هي لازمة مساوية لنقيض العرفية. وأما بحسب الكمية فليس شيء منها نقيضاً حقيقياً كما عرفت (شريف).
And the contradictory of the conditional general is the temporal possible, which is a proposition in which it is judged to negate necessity with respect to the description from the opposite side, as in our saying: 'Every person who has pleurisy possibly coughs at some times while he is afflicted.' This is because this is a simple proposition that has not been considered among the well-known simple propositions, yet it is needed for the contradictory of some well-known simple propositions. For the essential necessary proposition and its contradictory – namely the absolute possible – both are among the well-known simples, as are the perpetual and the absolute general. As for the conditional general, its contradictory is not among the well-known propositions, and similarly the contradictory of the conventional general. And the relation of the temporal possible to the conditional general is like the relation of the absolute possible to the necessary, in that it is truly the contradictory of the conditional general with respect to modality. And the relation of the temporal absolute to the conventional general is like the relation of the absolute general to the perpetual, in that it is not truly the contradictory of the conventional general with respect to modality, but rather it is a necessary equivalent to its contradictory. As for quantity, none of them is a true contradictory, as you have learned (Sharif).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage defines the negations of two more complex types of modal propositions: the conditional general (mashrūṭa ʿāmma) and the conventional general (ʿurfiyya ʿāmma). The negation of a conditional general is the temporal possible (ḥīniyya mumkina). The author gives an example: 'Every person with pleurisy possibly coughs at some times while afflicted.' This example illustrates a conditional general because it asserts possibility under a specific condition (being afflicted). The author then notes that this type of proposition, though needed for contradictions, is not among the well-known simple propositions, unlike the essential necessary and its contradictory, or the perpetual and absolute general. Next, he compares relations: the temporal possible is to the conditional general as the absolute possible is to the necessary (i.e., true contradiction in modality). The temporal absolute (ḥīniyya muṭlaqa) is to the conventional general as the absolute general is to the perpetual (i.e., not a true contradiction in modality but a necessary equivalent). Finally, he remarks that none of these are true contradictions with respect to quantity (i.e., they do not have the familiar quantifier-based contradiction relations).

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a conditional general is a temporal possible, and the contradictory of a conventional general is a temporal absolute, but the latter is only a necessary equivalent, not a true modal contradictory.

Contradictories of Absolute and Perpetual Propositions
Author explains contradiction of absolute and perpetual propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any general absolute or perpetual absolute proposition and explain why they are true contradictories.

Core Idea
The contradictory of an absolute is a perpetual, and vice versa, because negation flips temporal scope.

In this section, the author lays out the foundational rule for contradictories of simple temporal propositions. You will learn how to find the contradictory of a general absolute proposition (e.g., 'Some A is B at some time') and a perpetual absolute proposition (e.g., 'Every A is B at all times'). This is an immediate inference that preserves truth under contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
Determine whether the proposition is general absolute (al-muṭlaqa al-ʿāmma) or perpetual absolute (al-dāʾima al-muṭlaqa). The general absolute judges affirmation/selb without temporal restriction, while the perpetual absolute judges permanence.
The passage uses 'salb' for negation, but we focus on affirmation.
2
Apply the contradictory rule
For a general absolute affirmation, its contradictory is a perpetual absolute negation: if the affirmation is not true in the aggregate, the negation is perpetual. Conversely, for a perpetual absolute negation, its contradictory is a general absolute affirmation.
The author states: 'if the affirmation is not in the aggregate, the negation is perpetual.'
3
Test with an Islamic example
Take the proposition 'Every sale is permissible' (general absolute). Its contradictory is 'Some sale is not permissible perpetually' (perpetual absolute negation). Check: if it is not true that every sale is permissible at some time, then it is never true, i.e., perpetually not permissible.
This illustrates the logical equivalence.
4
Verify the symmetry
Note that the contradictory of a perpetual absolute affirmation is a general absolute negation, and vice versa. This symmetry is key to understanding immediate inferences in temporal logic.
The passage also mentions the corresponding case for negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التناقض السلب لكان إما دائم الإيجاب أو ثابتاً في بعض الأوقات دون بعض، وأيا ما كان يتحقق إطلاق الإيجاب. وكذلك دوام الإيجاب يناقضه رفع دوام الإيجاب، وإذا ارتفع دوام الإيجاب، فإما أن يدوم السلب أو يتحقق السلب في بعض الأوقات دون بعض، وعلى كلا التقديرين فإطلاق السلب لازم جزماً. و هكذا البيان في أن نقيض المطلقة العامة الدائمة المطلقة، فإنه إذا لم يكن الإيجاب في الجملة يلزم السلب دائماً، وإذا لم يكن السلب في الجملة يلزم الإيجاب دائماً. ونقيض المشروطة العامة الحينية الممكنة، وهي التي يحكم فيها بسلب الضرورة بحسب الوصف عن الجانب المخالف، كقولنا : «كل من به ذات الجنب يمكن أن يسعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوباً» وذلك لأن هذه قضيّة بسيطة لم تعتبر في القضايا البسيطة المشهورة واحتيج إليها في نقيض بعض البسائط المشهورة، فالقضية الضرورية الذاتية ونقيضها - أعني الممكنة العامة - كلتاهما من البسائط المشهورة وكذا الدائمة والمطلقة العامة؛ وأما المشروطة العامة فليس نقيضها من القضايا المشهورة، وكذا نقيض العرفية العامة. ونسبة الحينية الممكنة إلى المشروطة العامة كنسبة الممكنة العامة إلى الضرورية في أنها نقيض المشروطة حقيقة بحسب الجهة، ونسبة الحينية المطلقة إلى العرفية العامة كنسبة المطلقة العامة إلى الدائمة في أنها ليست نقيض العرفية حقيقة بحسب الجهة، بل هي لازمة مساوية لنقيض العرفية. وأما بحسب الكمية فليس شيء منها نقيضاً حقيقياً كما عرفت. نسبتها إلى المشروطة العامة كنسبة الممكنة العامة إلى الضرورية المطلقة، وكما أن الضرورية بحسب الذات تناقض سلب الضرورة بحسب الذات، كذلك الضرورة بحسب الوصف تناقض سلب الضرورة بحسب الوصف. ونقيض العرفية العامة الحينية المطلقة، وهي التي يحكم فيها بالثبوت أو السلب بالفعل في بعض أوقات وصف الموضوع، ومثالها ما مر من قولنا : «كل من به ذات الجنب يسعل بالفعل في بعض أوقات كونه مجنوباً»، ونسبتها إلى العرفية العامة كنسبة المطلقة إلى الدائمة، فكما أن الدوام بحسب الذات ينافي الإطلاق بحسبها كذلك الدوام بحسب الوصف ينافي الإطلاق بحسبه.
Contradiction: The negation is either perpetual affirmation or established in some times without others, and in either case the absoluteness of affirmation is realized. Similarly, the perpetuity of affirmation is contradicted by the raising of the perpetuity of affirmation, and if the perpetuity of affirmation is raised, then either the negation is perpetual or the negation is realized in some times without others, and on both estimates the absoluteness of negation is necessarily entailed. And likewise the explanation regarding the contradictory of the general absolute is the perpetual absolute: if the affirmation is not in the aggregate, the negation is perpetual; if the negation is not in the aggregate, the affirmation is perpetual. The contradictory of the general conditional is the possible-existential, which is a proposition that judges the negation of necessity according to description from the opposite side, like our statement: 'Everyone who has pleurisy can cough in some times of his being pleuritic.' This is because this is a simple proposition not considered among the well-known simple propositions, and there is need for it in the contradiction of some well-known simple propositions. So the essential necessary proposition and its contradictory—i.e., the general possible—both are among the well-known simple propositions; likewise the perpetual and the general absolute. As for the general conditional, its contradictory is not among the well-known propositions, and likewise the contradictory of the general conventional. The relation of the possible-existential to the general conditional is like the relation of the general possible to the necessary in that it is the true contradictory of the conditional with respect to mode; and the relation of the absolute-existential to the general conventional is like the relation of the general absolute to the perpetual in that it is not the true contradictory of the conventional with respect to mode, but rather it is a necessary equivalent to the contradictory of the conventional. As for quantity, none of them is a true contradictory as you have learned. Its relation to the general conditional is like the relation of the general possible to the absolute necessary; and just as the essential necessary contradicts the negation of the essential necessity, likewise the descriptive necessary contradicts the negation of descriptive necessity. The contradictory of the general conventional is the absolute-existential, which is a proposition that judges actual affirmation or negation in some times of the subject's description, and its example is our statement that has passed: 'Everyone who has pleurisy actually coughs in some times of his being pleuritic.' Its relation to the general conventional is like the relation of the absolute to the perpetual; for just as perpetuity with respect to essence contradicts absoluteness with respect to it, so perpetuity with respect to description contradicts absoluteness with respect to it.

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictions of various simple temporal-conditional propositions. It begins by explaining the general absolute: its contradictory is the perpetual absolute, since if affirmation is not always true, negation is always true, and vice versa. Then it introduces the general conditional and its contradictory, the possible-existential (ḥīniyya mumkina). The author notes that the latter is not among the well-known simple propositions but is needed to contradict the conditional. The relation between these is compared to that between the essential necessary and the general possible. Similarly, the contradictory of the general conventional is the absolute-existential (ḥīniyya muṭlaqa), which is not the true contradictory in mode but an equivalent. The passage emphasizes that in terms of quantity, these are not true contradictories. It concludes by analogizing the descriptive necessary to the essential necessary in how they relate to their negations. The examples use the medical condition 'pleurisy' (dhāt al-janb) to illustrate temporal qualifiers.

Contradictories of Conditional and Conventional Propositions
Author explains contradiction of conditional and conventional propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of a general conditional proposition and a general conventional proposition, and distinguish between true contradictories and equivalents.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conditional is a possible-existential; for a conventional, it's an absolute-existential, but these are not well-known simple propositions.

The author now addresses the less common temporal propositions: the general conditional (e.g., 'Every pleuritic person can cough while pleuritic') and the general conventional (e.g., 'Every pleuritic person actually coughs at some time'). Their contradictories are not among the well-known simple propositions but are introduced here: the possible-existential and the absolute-existential. Understanding these is crucial for complete mastery of temporal logic.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general conditional
A general conditional judges necessity under a description, e.g., 'Every person with pleurisy necessarily coughs at some time while pleuritic' (but it is possible that they don't). The contradictory must negate this necessity.
The author states its contradictory is the possible-existential, which judges possibility of the opposite.
2
Identify the possible-existential
The possible-existential (al-ḥīniyya al-mumkina) judges that a subject can have a property at some time under the description. For example, 'Every person with pleurisy can cough at some time while pleuritic' is the contradictory of the conditional necessity.
The author compares this to the relation between the essential necessary and the general possible.
3
Understand the general conventional
A general conventional judges actuality under a description, e.g., 'Every person with pleurisy actually coughs at some time while pleuritic.' Its contradictory is the absolute-existential (al-ḥīniyya al-muṭlaqa).
The absolute-existential judges that the subject actually has the property at some time, but not necessarily.
4
Distinguish real contradictory from equivalent
The author notes that the absolute-existential is not the true contradictory of the conventional with respect to mode; rather, it is a necessary equivalent. The true contradictory would involve mode, but due to temporal quantifiers, these are equivalent in truth value.
This nuance is important for precision in logic.

It begins by explaining the general absolute: its contradictory is the perpetual absolute, since if affirmation is not always true, negation is always true, and vice versa. Then it introduces the general conditional and its contradictory, the possible-existential (ḥīniyya mumkina). The author notes that the latter is not among the well-known simple propositions but is needed to contradict the conditional. The relation between these is compared to that between the essential necessary and the general possible. Similarly, the contradictory of the general conventional is the absolute-existential (ḥīniyya muṭlaqa), which is not the true contradictory in mode but an equivalent. The passage emphasizes that in terms of quantity, these are not true contradictories. It concludes by analogizing the descriptive necessary to the essential necessary in how they relate to their negations. The examples use the medical condition 'pleurisy' (dhāt al-janb) to illustrate temporal qualifiers.

Key Terms

الحينية الممكنة
العرفية العامة

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a general conditional is a possible-existential, and for a general conventional it is an absolute-existential, though the latter is only a necessary equivalent, not a true contradictory in mode.

The Contradictory of Compound Propositions
Author defines the contradictory of compound propositions as a disjunctive concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any universal compound proposition as a disjunction between the contradictories of its parts.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a compound is an ambiguous disjunction, not a simple proposition.

In this passage, the author explains how to find the contradictory of compound propositions, which are central to modal logic in Islamic thought. Understanding this rule prevents errors in negation when dealing with complex statements in kalam and usul al-fiqh. The key insight is that the contradictory is not a single simple proposition but a disjunctive concept that encompasses both possibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound proposition
Recognize that the proposition is composed of two simple propositions that differ in quality (affirmation/negation) or quantity. In the passage, the non-perpetual existential (al-wujūdiyya lā dāʾima) is a compound of two general absolutes: one affirmative and one negative.
2
Recall the contradictory rule for simple propositions
For simple absolute propositions, the contradictory is a perpetual proposition (dāʾima). The author reminds us that 'the contradictory of the absolute is the perpetual.'
3
Apply the rule for compound contradictory
The contradictory of a universal compound is one of the two contradictories of its parts, but without determination which one. That is, it is either the contradictory of the first part or the contradictory of the second part, but not specified.
This is because to negate the conjunction (the sum), you only need to negate one of the parts.
4
Analyze the example
For the non-perpetual existential (composed of an affirmative absolute and a negative absolute), its contradictory is either the perpetual differing (al-dāʾima al-mukhālifa) which is negative, or the perpetual agreeing (al-dāʾima al-muwāfiqa) which is affirmative. Both are possible.
5
Formulate the ambiguous concept
The contradictory is equivalent to a disjunctive concept (al-mafhūm al-muraddad) that hovers between the two contradictories of the parts. It is not a single proposition but a disjunction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

That is clear after grasping the realities of compounds and the contradictions of simples. For if you realize that the non-perpetual existential proposition is composed of two general absolutes, one affirmative and the other negative, and that the contradictory of the absolute is the perpetual, then you will realize that its contradictory is either the perpetual differing or the perpetual agreeing. For if its parts are realized, the sum is realized, and removing one of the parts is one of the two contradictories of the parts, not determinately. This passage defines the contradictory of compound propositions, which are composed of two simple propositions with opposite quantity/quality. The author states that for a universal compound, its contradictory is one of the contradictories of its two parts, but not determinately which. He illustrates with the example of the non-perpetual existential (al-wujūdiyya lā dāʾima), which combines two general absolutes: one affirmative and one negative. Since the contradictory of a general absolute is the perpetual (dāʾima), the contradictory of this compound is either a perpetual that opposes in quality (al-mukhālifa) or one that agrees (al-muwāfiqa). The explanation clarifies that raising the compound (its negation) is equivalent to raising one of its parts, but not specifying which; thus the negation is a disjunctive concept between the two contradictories of its parts. The passage emphasizes that the contradictory of a compound is not a simple proposition but an ambiguous (murakkab) notion.

Contradictory of Compound Propositions: General Method
Author explains method and proof for contradictory of compound propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the contradictory of any compound proposition by resolving it into its two simple parts and forming an exclusive disjunction of their contradictories.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conjunction is a disjunction—negating both parts is wrong.

In Islamic logic, compound propositions combine two simple propositions with opposite qualities (affirmation/negation). Their contradictory is not simply the conjunction of contradictories, but an exclusive disjunction (man'iat al-khuluw). This lesson walks through the definition, proof, and method for finding it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound structure
Recognize that a compound proposition (al-qadiyya al-murakkaba) is the conjunction (sum) of two propositions differing in affirmation and negation. For example, 'Every A is B and some A is not B' is compound.
Ensure both parts are simple propositions with opposite quality.
2
Understand negation of conjunction
The contradictory (naqid) of the sum is the negation of that sum. Negating a conjunction means at least one part must be negated, but not determinately which.
This is a key difference from the negation of a disjunction.
3
Form the disjunction of contradictories
The contradictory of each part is taken. Then these two contradictories are combined into an exclusive disjunction (man'iat al-khuluw): 'Either the contradictory of part1 or the contradictory of part2, but not both false'.
Exclusive disjunction requires at least one true (man'iat al-khuluw).
4
Verify equivalence via truth conditions
Check: If original is true, both parts true → both contradictories false → disjunction false. If original false, at least one part false → its contradictory true → disjunction true. Thus the disjunction is equivalent to the contradictory.
This proof is given in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وأما المركبات فإن كانت كلّية فنقيضها أحد نقيضي جزأيها وذلك جلي بعد الإحاطة بحقائق المركبات ونقائض البسائط، فإنك إذا تحققت أن الوجودية اللادائمة تركيبها من مطلقتين عامتين إحداهما موجبة والأخرى سالبة، وأن نقيض المطلقة هو الدائمة: تحققت أن نقيضها إما الدائمة المخالفة أو الدائمة الموافقة. القول : القضية المركبة عبارة عن مجموع قضيتين مختلفتين بالإيجاب والسلب، فنقيضها رفع ذلك المجموع؛ لكن رفع المجموع إنما يكون برفع أحد جزأيه لا على التعيين، فإن جزايه إذا تحققا تحقق المجموع، ورفع أحد الجزأين هو أحد نقيضي الجزأين لا على التعيين، فيكون لازماً مساوياً لنقيض المركبة، وهو المفهوم المردّد بين نقيضي الجزأين، لأن أحد النقيضين مفهوم مردّد بينهما، فيقال إمّا هذا النقيض وإما ذلك النقيض، وبالحقيقة هو منفصلة مانعة الخلو مركبة من نقيضي الجزأين. فيكون طريق أخذ نقيض المركبة أن تحلّل إلى بسيطيها، ويؤخذ لكلّ منهما نقيض وتركب منفصلة مانعة الخلو من النقيضين، فهي مساوية لنقيضها، لأنه متى صدق الأصل كذبت المنفصلة، لأنه متى صدق الأصل صدق جزاه، ومتى صدق الجزآن كذب نقيضاهما فتكذب المنفصلة المانعة الخلو لكذب جزأيها ، ومتى كذب الأصل صدقت المنفصلة، لأنه متى كذب الأصل فلابد أن يكذب أحد جزأيه ، ومتى كذب أحد جزأيه صدق نقيضه فتصدق المنفصلة لصدق أحد جزأيها. وذلك – أي طريق أخذ نقيض المركبة - جلي بعد الإحاطة بحقائق المركبات ونقائض البسائط، فإنّك إذا تحققت أن الوجودية اللادائمة مركبة من مطلقتين عامتين أولاهما موافقة للأصل في الكيف وأخراهما مخالفة له في الكيف، وتحققت أن نقيض المطلقة العامة الموافقة «الدائمة المخالفة»، ونقيض المطلقة العامة المخالفة «الدائمة الموافقة» : علمت أن نقيض الوجودية اللادائمة إما الدائمة المخالفة أو الدائمة الموافقة ; فإذا (١) ولما تحققت أن الوجودية اللاضروريّة مركبة من مطلقة عامة موافقة لأصل القضية في الكيف وممكنة عامة مخالفة له، وأن نقيض المطلقة العامة الموافقة الدائمة المخالفة ونقيض الممكنة المخالفة الضرورية الموافقة؛ فنقيض الوجودية اللاضرورية إما الدائمة المخالفة أو الضرورية الموافقة. وعلى هذا فنقيض المشروطة الخاصة إما الحينيّة الممكنة المخالفة أو الدائمة الموافقة.
He said: As for compound [propositions], if they are universal, their contradictory is one of the contradictories of their two parts—that is clear after comprehending the realities of compound [propositions] and the contradictories of simple ones. For if you realize that the existential non-permanent [proposition] is composed of two absolute general [propositions], one affirmative and the other negative, and that the contradictory of the absolute is the permanent, you realize that its contradictory is either the permanent contrary [in quality] or the permanent agreeing [in quality]. The statement: The compound proposition is an expression of a sum of two propositions differing in affirmation and negation, so its contradictory is the negation of that sum; but the negation of the sum is only by negating one of its parts indeterminately. For if its two parts are actual, the sum is actual, and the negation of one of the two parts is one of the contradictories of the two parts indeterminately. Thus it is a necessary equivalent to the contradictory of the compound, and it is the concept that is disjunctively between the contradictories of the two parts, because each of the two contradictories is a concept disjunctively between them. So it is said: either this contradictory or that contradictory, and in reality it is an exclusive disjunction composed of the contradictories of the two parts. Therefore the way to take the contradictory of a compound is to analyze it into its two simples, take the contradictory of each, and compose an exclusive disjunction from the two contradictories. It is equivalent to its contradictory because whenever the original is true, the disjunction is false. For whenever the original is true, its two parts are true, and whenever the two parts are true, their contradictories are false, so the exclusive disjunction is false due to the falsity of its two parts. And whenever the original is false, the disjunction is true, because whenever the original is false, necessarily one of its two parts is false, and whenever one of its two parts is false, its contradictory is true, so the disjunction is true due to the truth of one of its two parts. And that—i.e., the way to take the contradictory of a compound—is clear after comprehending the realities of compounds and the contradictories of simples. For if you realize that the existential non-permanent is composed of two absolute general [propositions], the first of which agrees with the original in quality and the last of which disagrees with it in quality, and you realize that the contradictory of the agreeing absolute general is the permanent contrary, and the contradictory of the disagreeing absolute general is the permanent agreeing, you know that the contradictory of the existential non-permanent is either the permanent contrary or the permanent agreeing. And likewise, if you realize that the existential non-necessary is composed of an absolute general agreeing with the original proposition in quality and a possible general disagreeing with it, and that the contradictory of the agreeing absolute general is the permanent contrary, and the contradictory of the disagreeing possible is the necessary agreeing, then the contradictory of the existential non-necessary is either the permanent contrary or the necessary agreeing. And similarly, the contradictory of the special conditioned is either the temporary possible contrary or the permanent agreeing.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage explains how to find the contradictory (naqid) of a compound proposition. The author begins by stating that for universal compound propositions, the contradictory is one of the contradictories of its two parts, taken indeterminately. This becomes clear once one understands natures of compound propositions and the contradictories of simple ones. He illustrates with the example of the 'existential non-permanent' (al-wujudiyya al-la-da'ima). This proposition is composed of two absolute general (mutlaqa 'amma) propositions: one affirmative and one negative. The contradictory of an absolute proposition is the permanent (da'ima) proposition. Therefore, the contradictory of the existential non-permanent is either the permanent that is opposite in quality (mukhalifa) or the permanent that agrees in quality (muwafiq).

He then gives a general definition: a compound proposition is the conjunction (jumla) of two propositions differing in affirmation and negation. Its contradictory is the negation of that conjunction. The negation of a conjunction is achieved by negating one of its parts, but not determinately—i.e., it is a disjunction of the negations. So the contradictory of the compound is a concept that is disjunctively between the contradictories of the two parts. This is actually an exclusive disjunction (man'iat al-khuluw) composed of the contradictories of the parts.

The method to find the contradictory is: resolve the compound into its two simple propositions, find the contradictory of each, and compose a disjunction that is exclusive (man'iat al-khuluw). This disjunction is equivalent to the contradictory of the original compound. Proof: If the original is true, both its parts are true, so their contradictories are false, making the disjunction false. If the original is false, at least one part is false, so its contradictory is true, making the disjunction true.

Finally, he applies this method to the existential non-permanent, showing its two parts are an absolute general agreeing in quality and another disagreeing. The contradictory of the agreeing absolute is the permanent contrary (da'ima mukhalifa), and of the disagreeing absolute is the permanent agreeing (da'ima muwafiq). Hence, the contradictory is a disjunction of these two. Similarly, for the existential non-necessary and the special conditioned (mashruta khassa), he gives analogous results. The passage thus provides a clear procedure for transforming compound modal propositions into their logical contradictories, which is essential for constructing valid syllogisms and dialectical arguments.

Key Terms
القضية المركبة
منفصلة مانعة الخلو
نقيض

C) A disjunction of the parts themselves.
D) The contradictory of only one part.

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a compound proposition (conjunction) is an exclusive disjunction of the contradictories of its two parts, not a conjunction of negations.

Applying the Method: Modal Compound Examples
Author gives examples of finding contradictories for modal compounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the contradictory of specific modal compound propositions like 'existential non-permanent' using the method of resolving into simples and forming an exclusive disjunction.

Core Idea
Modal compounds like 'existential non-permanent' are conjunctions of absolute propositions - their contradictories are disjunctions of permanent propositions.

The passage illustrates the general method with three modal examples: existential non-permanent, existential non-necessary, and special conditioned. This lesson focuses on the first two, showing how to apply the decomposition and disjunction formation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the modal compound structure
Identify that 'existential non-permanent' (al-wujudiyya al-la-da'ima) means 'exists but not permanently'. It is compound: it asserts existence (affirmative absolute) and denies permanence (negative absolute). So it is a conjunction of an affirmative absolute and a negative absolute.
The two parts differ in quality (affirmative vs negative).
2
Determine the contradictories of the parts
The contradictory of an absolute general proposition is a permanent proposition (da'ima). Specifically, the contradictory of an affirmative absolute is a negative permanent (mukhalifa), and of a negative absolute is an affirmative permanent (muwafiq).
These are derived from earlier sections on simple propositions.
3
Form the exclusive disjunction
Combine the two contradictories into an exclusive disjunction: 'Either the permanent contrary (da'ima mukhalifa) or the permanent agreeing (da'ima muwafiq)'. This is the contradictory of the original compound.
The disjunction must be exclusive (man'iat al-khuluw) - at least one true, not both false.
4
Apply to existential non-necessary
Similarly, 'existential non-necessary' is compound of an affirmative absolute and a negative possible. Its contradictory is: 'Either the permanent contrary (contradictory of affirming absolute) or the necessary agreeing (contradictory of negative possible)'.
The contradictories of modal simples are predetermined by rules.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
